## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Stress typically increases nonlinearly with strain (hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening), often modeled with multiplicative decomposition.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (T-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (linear elastic with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Hollomon power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (power-law strain hardening at fixed T)
- Johnson-Cook (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal term)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T**c4) (hardening with power-law thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal factor)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening model)
- Voce + thermal: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (1 + c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Ludwik + thermal: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik with exponential thermal softening)
- Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law, avoids zero-strain singularity)
- Swift + thermal: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (1 + c3 * T) (Swift with linear thermal correction)
- Zerilli-Armstrong type: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (thermally activated dislocation model)
- Rational thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * c2 / (T + c3) (inverse temperature dependence)
- Combined exponential: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (Voce hardening with Arrhenius thermal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain hardening and thermal softening → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), reflecting independent mechanisms
- Power-law strain hardening ε^n with n typically between 0.1 and 0.5 → reflects dislocation density evolution in metals
- Saturating/Voce-type hardening (1 - exp(-c*ε)) → indicates dynamic recovery balancing work hardening at large strains
- Arrhenius-type thermal factor exp(-Q/T) or exp(c*T) → thermally activated deformation processes (dislocation climb, diffusion)
- Shifted power law (ε + ε₀)^n → avoids singularity at zero strain and accounts for pre-strain or initial dislocation density
- Polynomial thermal correction (1 - c*T^m) with m>1 → accelerated softening near melting point
- Additive yield stress term (c₀ + f(ε)) → separation of initial yield strength from strain-dependent hardening
- Inverse temperature dependence c/(T + c₁) → characteristic of thermally activated rate processes at moderate temperatures
